	<div id="right-col">

		<div id="content" role="main" class="widthfix">
			<h1 class="page-title">Electrical Engineering and Computer Science (Course 6)</h1>




<div id="textcontainer" class="tab_content">



</div><!--end #textcontainer -->

			<div id="coursestextcontainer" >
				<a name="coursestext"></a><div id="sc_sccoursedescs">
<h2 class="sectionhead">Basic Undergraduate Subjects</h2><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.00 Introduction to Computer Science and Programming</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: None
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-7-2 units. REST</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to computer science and programming for students with little or no programming experience. Students learn how to program and how to use computational techniques to solve problems. Topics include software design, algorithms, data analysis, and simulation techniques. Assignments are done using the Python programming language. Meets with <a href="/search/?P=6.0001" title="6.0001" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0001');">6.0001</a> first half of term and <a href="/search/?P=6.0002" title="6.0002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0002');">6.0002</a> second half of term. Credit cannot also be received for <a href="/search/?P=6.0001" title="6.0001" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0001');">6.0001</a> or <a href="/search/?P=6.0002" title="6.0002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0002');">6.0002</a>. Final given during final exam week.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. V. Guttag
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.0001 Introduction to Computer Science Programming in Python</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: None
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring; first half of term)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">2-3-1 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to computer science and programming for students with little or no programming experience. Students develop skills to program and use computational techniques to solve problems. Topics include the notion of computation, Python, simple algorithms and data structures, testing and debugging, and algorithmic complexity. Combination of <a href="/search/?P=6.0001" title="6.0001" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0001');">6.0001</a> and <a href="/search/?P=6.0002" title="6.0002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0002');">6.0002</a> counts as REST subject. Final given in the seventh week of the term.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. V. Guttag
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.0002 Introduction to Computational Thinking and Data Science</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.0001" title="6.0001" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0001');">6.0001</a> or permission of instructor
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring; second half of term)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">2-3-1 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Provides an introduction to using computation to understand real-world phenomena. Topics include plotting, stochastic programs, probability and statistics, random walks, Monte Carlo simulations, modeling data, optimization problems, and clustering. Combination of <a href="/search/?P=6.0001" title="6.0001" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0001');">6.0001</a> and <a href="/search/?P=6.0002" title="6.0002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0002');">6.0002</a> counts as REST subject. Final given during final exam week.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. V. Guttag
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.002 Circuits and Electronics</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=8.02|8.021|8.022" onclick="return showCourse(this, '8.02|8.021|8.022');">Physics II (GIR)</a>; <i>Coreq: <a href="/search/?P=18.03" title="18.03" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.03');">18.03</a> or <a href="/search/?P=2.087" title="2.087" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '2.087');">2.087</a></i>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-1-7 units. REST</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Fundamentals of the lumped circuit abstraction. Resistive elements and networks, independent and dependent sources, switches and MOS devices, digital abstraction, amplifiers, and energy storage elements. Dynamics of first- and second-order networks; design in the time and frequency domains; analog and digital circuits and applications. Design exercises. Occasional laboratory.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>A. Agarwal, J. del Alamo, J. H. Lang, D. J. Perreault
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.003 Signals and Systems</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=8.02|8.021|8.022" onclick="return showCourse(this, '8.02|8.021|8.022');">Physics II (GIR)</a>; <a href="/search/?P=2.087" title="2.087" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '2.087');">2.087</a> or <a href="/search/?P=18.03" title="18.03" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.03');">18.03</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">5-0-7 units. REST</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Presents the fundamentals of signal and system analysis. Topics include discrete-time and continuous-time signals, Fourier series and transforms, Laplace and Z transforms, and analysis of linear, time-invariant systems. Applications drawn broadly from engineering and physics, including audio and image processing, communications, and automatic control.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>D. M. Freeman, Q. Hu, J. S. Lim
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.004 Computation Structures</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=8.02|8.021|8.022" onclick="return showCourse(this, '8.02|8.021|8.022');">Physics II (GIR)</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units. REST</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduces architecture of digital systems, emphasizing structural principles common to a wide range of technologies. Multilevel implementation strategies; definition of new primitives (e.g., gates, instructions, procedures, and processes) and their mechanization using lower-level elements. Analysis of potential concurrency; precedence constraints and performance measures; pipelined and multidimensional systems. Instruction set design issues; architectural support for contemporary software structures.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>S. A. Ward, C. J. Terman
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.005 Elements of Software Construction</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.01" title="6.01" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.01');">6.01</a>; <i>Coreq: <a href="/search/?P=6.042" title="6.042[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.042');">6.042[J]</a></i>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units. REST</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduces fundamental principles and techniques of software development, i.e., how to write software that is safe from bugs, easy to understand, and ready for change. Topics include specifications and invariants; testing, test-case generation, and coverage; abstract data types and representation independence; design patterns for object-oriented programming; concurrent programming, including message passing and shared concurrency, and defending against races and deadlock; and functional programming with immutable data and higher-order functions. Includes weekly programming exercises and larger group programming projects. 12 Engineering Design Points.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>D. N. Jackson, R. C. Miller
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.006 Introduction to Algorithms</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.042" title="6.042[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.042');">6.042[J]</a>; <a href="/search/?P=6.01" title="6.01" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.01');">6.01</a> or <i>Coreq: <a href="/search/?P=6.009" title="6.009" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.009');">6.009</a></i>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to mathematical modeling of computational problems, as well as common algorithms, algorithmic paradigms, and data structures used to solve these problems. Emphasizes the relationship between algorithms and programming, and introduces basic performance measures and analysis techniques for these problems.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>R. L. Rivest, S. Devadas
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.007 Electromagnetic Energy: From Motors to Solar Cells</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=8.02|8.021|8.022" onclick="return showCourse(this, '8.02|8.021|8.022');">Physics II (GIR)</a>; <i>Coreq: <a href="/search/?P=2.087" title="2.087" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '2.087');">2.087</a> or <a href="/search/?P=18.03" title="18.03" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.03');">18.03</a></i>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">5-1-6 units. REST</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Discusses applications of electromagnetic and equivalent quantum mechanical principles to classical and modern devices. Covers energy conversion and power flow in both macroscopic and quantum-scale electrical and electromechanical systems, including electric motors and generators, electric circuit elements, quantum tunneling structures and instruments. Studies photons as waves and particles and their interaction with matter in optoelectronic devices, including solar cells and displays.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>V. Bulovic, R. J. Ram
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.008 Introduction to Inference</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=18.02|18.02A|18.022|18.024" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.02|18.02A|18.022|18.024');">Calculus II (GIR)</a> or permission of instructor
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-4-4 units. Institute LAB</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduces probabilistic modeling for problems of inference and machine learning from data, emphasizing analytical and computational aspects. Distributions, marginalization, conditioning, and structure; graphical representations. Belief propagation, decision-making, classification, estimation, and prediction. Sampling methods and analysis. Introduces asymptotic analysis and information measures. Substantial computational laboratory component explores the concepts introduced in class in the context of realistic contemporary applications. Students design inference algorithms, investigate their behavior on real data, and discuss experimental results.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>P. Golland, G. W. Wornell
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.009 Fundamentals of Programming (6.S04)</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.0001" title="6.0001" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0001');">6.0001</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">2-4-6 units. Institute LAB</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduces fundamental concepts of programming. Designed to develop skills in applying basic methods from programming languages to abstract problems. Topics include programming and Python basics, computational concepts, software engineering, algorithmic techniques, data types, and recursion and tail recursion. Lab component consists of software design, construction, and implementation of design.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>A. Chlipala, S. Devadas
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.01 Introduction to EECS via Robot Sensing, Software and Control</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.0001" title="6.0001" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0001');">6.0001</a> or permission of instructor
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">2-4-6 units. Institute LAB</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">An integrated introduction to electrical engineering and computer science, taught using substantial laboratory experiments with mobile robots. Key issues in the design of engineered artifacts operating in the natural world: measuring and modeling system behaviors; assessing errors in sensors and effectors; specifying tasks; designing solutions based on analytical and computational models; planning, executing, and evaluating experimental tests of performance; refining models and designs. Issues addressed in the context of computer programs, control systems, probabilistic inference problems, circuits and transducers, which all play important roles in achieving robust operation of a large variety of engineered systems.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>D. M. Freeman, A. Hartz, L. P. Kaelbling, T. Lozano-Perez
</i></span></p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.011 Signals, Systems and Inference</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.003" title="6.003" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.003');">6.003</a>; <a href="/search/?P=6.008" title="6.008" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.008');">6.008</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.041A" title="6.041A" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041A');">6.041A</a>, or <a href="/search/?P=18.600" title="18.600" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.600');">18.600</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Covers signals, systems and inference in communication, control and signal processing. Topics include input-output and state-space models of linear systems driven by deterministic and random signals; time- and transform-domain representations in discrete and continuous time; and group delay. State feedback and observers. Probabilistic models; stochastic processes, correlation functions, power spectra, spectral factorization. Least-mean square error estimation; Wiener filtering. Hypothesis testing; detection; matched filters.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>A. V. Oppenheim, G. C. Verghese
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.012 Microelectronic Devices and Circuits</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.002" title="6.002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.002');">6.002</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Microelectronic device modeling, and basic microelectronic circuit analysis and design. Physical electronics of semiconductor junction and MOS devices. Relating terminal behavior to internal physical processes, developing circuit models, and understanding the uses and limitations of different models. Use of incremental and large-signal techniques to analyze and design transistor circuits, with examples chosen from digital circuits, linear amplifiers, and other integrated circuits. Design project.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>A. I. Akinwande, D. A. Antoniadis, J. Kong, C. G. Sodini
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.013 Electromagnetics and Applications</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=18.02|18.02A|18.022|18.024" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.02|18.02A|18.022|18.024');">Calculus II (GIR)</a>, <a href="/search/?P=8.02|8.021|8.022" onclick="return showCourse(this, '8.02|8.021|8.022');">Physics II (GIR)</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-3-6 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Analysis and design of modern applications that employ electromagnetic phenomena for signals and power transmission in RF, microwaves, optical and wireless communication systems. Fundamentals include dynamic solutions for Maxwell's equations; electromagnetic power and energy, waves in media, guided waves, radiation, and diffraction; coupling to media and structures; resonance &amp; filters; acoustic analogs. Labs include student hands-on activities from building to testing of devices and systems (e.g. radar) that reinforce lectures, with a focus on fostering creativity and debugging skills. <a href="/search/?P=6.002" title="6.002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.002');">6.002</a> and <a href="/search/?P=6.007" title="6.007" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.007');">6.007</a> are recommended but not required.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>L. Daniel, M. R. Watts
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.02 Introduction to EECS via Communications Networks</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.0001" title="6.0001" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.0001');">6.0001</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-4-4 units. Institute LAB</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Studies key concepts, systems, and algorithms to reliably communicate data in settings ranging from the cellular phone network and the Internet to deep space. Weekly laboratory experiments explore these areas in depth. Topics presented in three modules - bits, signals, and packets - spanning the multiple layers of a communication system. Bits module includes information, entropy, data compression algorithms, and error correction with block and convolutional codes. Signals module includes modeling physical channels and noise, signal design, filtering and detection, modulation, and frequency-division multiplexing. Packets module includes switching and queuing principles, media access control, routing protocols, and data transport protocols.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>H. Balakrishnan, K. LaCurts, G. C. Verghese,
</i></span></p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Integrated overview of the biophysics of cells from prokaryotes to neurons, with a focus on mass transport and electrical signal generation across cell membrane. First half of course focuses on mass transport through membranes: diffusion, osmosis, chemically mediated, and active transport. Second half focuses on electrical properties of cells: ion transport to action potentials in electrically excitable cells. Synaptic transmission. Electrical properties interpreted via kinetic and molecular properties of single voltage-gated ion channels. Laboratory and computer exercises illustrate the concepts. Students taking graduate version complete different assignments.
Preference to juniors and seniors.</p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.037 Structure and Interpretation of Computer Programs</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: None
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (IAP)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">1-0-5 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Studies the structure and interpretation of computer programs which transcend specific programming languages. Demonstrates thought patterns for computer science using Scheme. Includes weekly programming projects.
Enrollment may be limited.</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>Staff
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.041A Introduction to Probability I (New)</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Subject meets with <a href="/search/?P=6.431A" title="6.431A" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.431A');">6.431A</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=18.02|18.02A|18.022|18.024" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.02|18.02A|18.022|18.024');">Calculus II (GIR)</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring; first half of term)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">2-0-4 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Provides an introduction to probability theory and the modeling and analysis of probabilistic systems. Probabilistic models, conditional probability. Discrete and continuous random variables. Expectation and conditional expectation. Limit Theorems. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments. Combination of <a href="/search/?P=6.041A" title="6.041A" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041A');">6.041A</a> and <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a> counts as a REST subject.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>P. Jaillet, J. N. Tsitsiklis
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.041B Introduction to Probability II (New)</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Subject meets with <a href="/search/?P=6.431B" title="6.431B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.431B');">6.431B</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.041A" title="6.041A" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041A');">6.041A</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring; second half of term)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">2-0-4 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Building on <a href="/search/?P=6.041A" title="6.041A" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041A');">6.041A</a>, further discusses topics in probability. Bayesian estimation and hypothesis testing. Elements of statistical inference. Bernoulli and Poisson processes. Markov chains. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments. Combination of <a href="/search/?P=6.041A" title="6.041A" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041A');">6.041A</a> and <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a> counts as a REST subject.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>P. Jaillet, J. N. Tsitsiklis
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.042[J] Mathematics for Computer Science</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=18.062J" title="18.062[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.062J');">18.062[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=18.01|18.01A|18.014" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.01|18.01A|18.014');">Calculus I (GIR)</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">5-0-7 units. REST</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Elementary discrete mathematics for computer science and engineering. Emphasis on mathematical definitions and proofs as well as on applicable methods. Topics include formal logic notation, proof methods; induction, well-ordering; sets, relations; elementary graph theory; asymptotic notation and growth of functions; permutations and combinations, counting principles; discrete probability. Further selected topics include recursive definition and structural induction, state machines and invariants, integer congruences, recurrences, generating functions.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>F. T. Leighton, A. R. Meyer, A. Moitra
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.045[J] Automata, Computability, and Complexity</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=18.400J" title="18.400[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.400J');">18.400[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.042" title="6.042[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.042');">6.042[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Provides an introduction to some of the central ideas of theoretical computer science, including circuits, finite automata, Turing machines and computability, efficient algorithms and reducibility, the P versus NP problem, NP-completeness, the power of randomness, cryptography, computational learning theory, and quantum computing. Examines the classes of problems that can and cannot be solved in various computational models.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>S. Aaronson
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.046[J] Design and Analysis of Algorithms</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=18.410J" title="18.410[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.410J');">18.410[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.006" title="6.006" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.006');">6.006</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Techniques for the design and analysis of efficient algorithms, emphasizing methods useful in practice. Topics include sorting; search trees, heaps, and hashing; divide-and-conquer; dynamic programming; greedy algorithms; amortized analysis; graph algorithms; and shortest paths. Advanced topics may include network flow; computational geometry; number-theoretic algorithms; polynomial and matrix calculations; caching; and parallel computing.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>E. Demaine, M. Goemans
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.047 Computational Biology: Genomes, Networks, Evolution</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Subject meets with <a href="/search/?P=6.878J" title="6.878[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.878J');">6.878[J]</a>, <a href="/search/?P=HST.507J" title="HST.507[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, 'HST.507J');">HST.507[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.006" title="6.006" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.006');">6.006</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a>, <a href="/search/?P=7.012|7.013|7.014|7.015|7.016" onclick="return showCourse(this, '7.012|7.013|7.014|7.015|7.016');">Biology (GIR)</a>; or permission of instructor
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Covers the algorithmic and machine learning foundations of computational biology, combining theory with practice. Principles of algorithm design, influential problems and techniques, and analysis of large-scale biological datasets. Topics include (a) genomes: sequence analysis, gene finding, RNA folding, genome alignment and assembly, database search; (b) networks: gene expression analysis, regulatory motifs, biological network analysis; (c) evolution: comparative genomics, phylogenetics, genome duplication, genome rearrangements, evolutionary theory. These are coupled with fundamental algorithmic techniques including: dynamic programming, hashing, Gibbs sampling, expectation maximization, hidden Markov models, stochastic context-free grammars, graph clustering, dimensionality reduction, Bayesian networks.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>M. Kellis
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.050[J] Information, Entropy, and Computation</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=2.110J" title="2.110[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '2.110J');">2.110[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=8.01|8.01L|8.011|8.012" onclick="return showCourse(this, '8.01|8.01L|8.011|8.012');">Physics I (GIR)</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-6 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Explores the ultimate limits to communication and computation, with an emphasis on the physical nature of information and information processing. Topics include information and computation, digital signals, codes, and compression. Biological representations of information. Logic circuits, computer architectures, and algorithmic information. Noise, probability, and error correction. The concept of entropy applied to channel capacity and to the second law of thermodynamics. Reversible and irreversible operations and the physics of computation. Quantum computation.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>P. Penfield, Jr., S. Lloyd
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.061 Introduction to Electric Power Systems</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Subject meets with <a href="/search/?P=6.690" title="6.690" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.690');">6.690</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.002" title="6.002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.002');">6.002</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.013" title="6.013" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.013');">6.013</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">Acad Year 2016-2017: U (Spring)<br/>
Acad Year 2017-2018: Not offered
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Electric circuit theory with application to power handling electric circuits. Modeling and behavior of electromechanical devices, including magnetic circuits, motors, and generators. Operational fundamentals of synchronous, induction and DC machinery. Interconnection of generators and motors with electric power transmission and distribution circuits. Power generation, including alternative and sustainable sources. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. L. Kirtley, Jr.
</i></span></p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.070[J] Electronics Project Laboratory</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=EC.120J" title="EC.120[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, 'EC.120J');">EC.120[J]</a>

</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">2-2-2 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Intuition-based introduction to electronics, electronic components and test equipment such as oscilloscopes, meters (voltage, resistance inductance, capacitance, etc.), and signal generators. Emphasizes individual instruction and development of skills, such as soldering, assembly, and troubleshooting. Students design, build, and keep a small electronics project to put their new knowledge into practice. Intended for students with little or no previous background in electronics.
Enrollment may be limited.</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. Bales
</i></span></p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.S08 Special Subject: Interconnected Embedded Systems</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: None
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">1-5-6 units. Institute LAB</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to embedded systems in the context of connected devices, wearables and the &quot;Internet of Things&quot;. Topics include microcontrollers, energy utilization, algorithmic efficiency, interfacing with sensors, networking, cryptography, local versus distributed computation, data analytics, and 3D printing. Students will design, make, and program an internet-connected wearable device. Final project where student teams will design and demo their own cloud-connected wearable system. Licensed for Spring 2016 by the Committee on Curricula.
Enrollment limited; preference to first- and second-year students.</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. Voldman, J. D. Steinmeyer
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">

</div><h2 class="sectionhead">Undergraduate Laboratory Subjects</h2><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.100 Electrical Engineering and Computer Science Project</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: None
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring, Summer)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">Units arranged</span><br/><span class="courseblockoptional">Can be repeated for credit.</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Individual experimental work related to electrical engineering and computer science. Student must make arrangements with a project supervisor and file a proposal endorsed by the supervisor. Departmental approval required. Written report to be submitted upon completion of work.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>Consult Department Undergraduate Office
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.101 Introductory Analog Electronics Laboratory</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.002" title="6.002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.002');">6.002</a> or 6.071
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">2-9-1 units. Institute LAB</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introductory experimental laboratory explores the design, construction, and debugging of analog electronic circuits. Lectures and laboratory projects in the first half of the course investigate the performance characteristics of semiconductor devices (diodes, BJTs, and MOSFETs) and functional analog building blocks, including single-stage amplifiers, op amps, small audio amplifier, filters, converters, sensor circuits, and medical electronics (ECG, pulse-oximetry). Projects involve design, implementation, and presentation in an environment similar to that of industry engineering design teams. Instruction and practice in written and oral communication provided. Opportunity to simulate real-world problems and solutions that involve tradeoffs and the use of engineering judgment. Engineers from local companies help students with their design projects.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>G. Hom
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.111 Introductory Digital Systems Laboratory</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.002" title="6.002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.002');">6.002</a>,  6.071, or <a href="/search/?P=16.004" title="16.004" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '16.004');">16.004</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-7-2 units. Institute LAB</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Lectures and labs on digital logic, flip flops, PALs, FPGAs, counters, timing, synchronization, and finite-state machines prepare students for the design and implementation of a final project of their choice: games, music, digital filters, wireless communications, video, or graphics. Extensive use of Verilog for describing and implementing digital logic designs.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>A. P. Chandrakasan, G. P. Hom
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.115 Microcomputer Project Laboratory</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Subject meets with <a href="/search/?P=6.1151" title="6.1151" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.1151');">6.1151</a>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduces analysis and design of embedded systems. Microcontrollers provide adaptation, flexibility, and real-time control. Emphasizes construction of complete systems, including a five-axis robot arm, a fluorescent lamp ballast, a tomographic imaging station (e.g., a CAT scan), and a simple calculator. Presents a wide range of basic tools, including software and development tools, programmable system on chip, peripheral components such as A/D converters, communication schemes, signal processing techniques, closed-loop digital feedback control, interface and power electronics, and modeling of electromechanical systems. Includes a sequence of assigned projects, followed by a final project of the student's choice, emphasizing creativity and uniqueness. Provides instruction in written and oral communication. <h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.152[J] Micro/Nano Processing Technology</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=3.155J" title="3.155[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '3.155J');">3.155[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: Permission of instructor
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-4-5 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduces the theory and technology of micro/nano fabrication. Lectures and laboratory sessions on basic processing techniques such as vacuum processes, lithography, diffusion, oxidation, and pattern transfer. Students fabricate MOS capacitors, nanomechanical cantilevers, and microfluidic mixers. Emphasis on the interrelationships between material properties and processing, device structure, and the electrical, mechanical, optical, chemical or biological behavior of devices. Provides background for thesis work in micro/nano fabrication. Students engage in extensive written and oral communication exercises.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>L. F. Velasquez-Garcia, J. Michel
</i></span></p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.161 Modern Optics Project Laboratory</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Subject meets with <a href="/search/?P=6.637" title="6.637" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.637');">6.637</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.003" title="6.003" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.003');">6.003</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-5-4 units. Institute LAB</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Lectures, laboratory exercises and projects on optical signal generation, transmission, detection, storage, processing and display. Topics include polarization properties of light; reflection and refraction; coherence and interference; Fraunhofer and Fresnel diffraction; holography; Fourier optics; coherent and incoherent imaging and signal processing systems; optical properties of materials; lasers and LEDs; electro-optic and acousto-optic light modulators; photorefractive and liquid-crystal light modulation; display technologies; optical waveguides and fiber-optic communication systems; photodetectors. Students may use this subject to find an advanced undergraduate project. Students engage in extensive oral and written communcation exercises. Recommended prerequisites: <a href="/search/?P=6.007" title="6.007" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.007');">6.007</a> or <a href="/search/?P=8.03" title="8.03" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '8.03');">8.03</a>.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>C. Warde
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.163 Strobe Project Laboratory</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=8.02|8.021|8.022" onclick="return showCourse(this, '8.02|8.021|8.022');">Physics II (GIR)</a> or permission of instructor
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall, Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">2-8-2 units. Institute LAB</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Application of electronic flash sources to measurement and photography. First half covers fundamentals of photography and electronic flashes, including experiments on application of electronic flash to photography, stroboscopy, motion analysis, and high-speed videography. Students write four extensive lab reports. In the second half, students work in small groups to select, design, and execute independent projects in measurement or photography that apply learned techniques. Project planning and execution skills are discussed and developed over the term. Students engage in extensive written and oral communication exercises.
Enrollment limited.</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. K. Vandiver, J. W. Bales
</i></span></p>

</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-8-1 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Illustrates a constructive (as opposed to a descriptive) approach to computer architecture. Topics include combinational and pipelined arithmetic-logic units (ALU), in-order pipelined microarchitectures, branch prediction, blocking and unblocking caches, interrupts, virtual memory support, cache coherence and multicore architectures. Labs in a modern Hardware Design Language (HDL) illustrate various aspects of microprocessor design, culminating in a term project in which students present a multicore design running on an FPGA board.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>Arvind
</i></span></p>

<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=14.15J" title="14.15[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '14.15J');">14.15[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a> or <a href="/search/?P=14.30" title="14.30" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '14.30');">14.30</a>

<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>Consult Department Headquarters
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.231 Dynamic Programming and Stochastic Control</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a> or <a href="/search/?P=18.204" title="18.204" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.204');">18.204</a>; <a href="/search/?P=18.100A" title="18.100A" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.100A');">18.100A</a>, <a href="/search/?P=18.100B" title="18.100B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.100B');">18.100B</a>, or <a href="/search/?P=18.100Q" title="18.100Q" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.100Q');">18.100Q</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Sequential decision-making via dynamic programming. Unified approach to optimal control of stochastic dynamic systems and Markovian decision problems. Applications in linear-quadratic control, inventory control, resource allocation, scheduling, and planning. Optimal decision making under perfect and imperfect state information. Certainty equivalent, open loop-feedback control, rollout, model predictive control, aggregation, and other suboptimal control methods. Infinite horizon problems: discounted, stochastic shortest path, average cost, and semi-Markov models. Value and policy iteration. Abstract models in dynamic programming. Approximate/neurodynamic programming. Simulation based methods. Discussion of current research on the solution of large-scale problems.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. N. Tsitsiklis
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.241[J] Dynamic Systems and Control</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=16.338J" title="16.338[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '16.338J');">16.338[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.003" title="6.003" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.003');">6.003</a>, <a href="/search/?P=18.06" title="18.06" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.06');">18.06</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Linear, discrete- and continuous-time, multi-input-output systems in control, related areas. Least squares and matrix perturbation problems. State-space models, modes, stability, controllability, observability, transfer function matrices, poles and zeros, and minimality. Internal stability of interconnected systems, feedback compensators, state feedback, optimal regulation, observers, and observer-based compensators. Measures of control performance, robustness issues using singular values of transfer functions. Introductory ideas on nonlinear systems. Recommended prerequisite: <a href="/search/?P=6.302" title="6.302" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.302');">6.302</a>.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>M. A. Dahleh, A. Megretski, E. Frazzoli
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.245 Multivariable Control Systems</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.241" title="6.241[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.241');">6.241[J]</a> or <a href="/search/?P=16.31" title="16.31" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '16.31');">16.31</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">Acad Year 2016-2017: Not offered<br/>
Acad Year 2017-2018: G (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Computer-aided design methodologies for synthesis of multivariable feedback control systems. Performance and robustness trade-offs. Model-based compensators; Q-parameterization; ill-posed optimization problems; dynamic augmentation; linear-quadratic optimization of controllers; H-infinity controller design; Mu-synthesis; model and compensator simplification; nonlinear effects. Computer-aided (MATLAB) design homework using models of physical processes.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>A. Megretski
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.251[J] Introduction to Mathematical Programming</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=15.081J" title="15.081[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '15.081J');">15.081[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=18.06" title="18.06" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.06');">18.06</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to linear optimization and its extensions emphasizing both methodology and the underlying mathematical structures and geometrical ideas. Covers classical theory of linear programming as well as some recent advances in the field. Topics: simplex method; duality theory; sensitivity analysis; network flow problems; decomposition; integer programming; interior point algorithms for linear programming; and introduction to combinatorial optimization and NP-completeness.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. N. Tsitsiklis, D. Bertsimas
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.252[J] Nonlinear Optimization</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=15.084J" title="15.084[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '15.084J');">15.084[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=18.06" title="18.06" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.06');">18.06</a>; <a href="/search/?P=18.100A" title="18.100A" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.100A');">18.100A</a>, <a href="/search/?P=18.100B" title="18.100B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.100B');">18.100B</a>, or 18.100C
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Unified analytical and computational approach to nonlinear optimization problems. Unconstrained optimization methods include gradient, conjugate direction, Newton, sub-gradient and first-order methods. Constrained optimization methods include feasible directions, projection, interior point methods, and Lagrange multiplier methods. Convex analysis, Lagrangian relaxation, nondifferentiable optimization, and applications in integer programming. Comprehensive treatment of optimality conditions and Lagrange multipliers. Geometric approach to duality theory. Applications drawn from control, communications, power systems, and resource allocation problems.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>R. M. Freund, D. P. Bertsekas, G. Perakis
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.253 Convex Analysis and Optimization</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=18.06" title="18.06" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.06');">18.06</a>; <a href="/search/?P=18.100A" title="18.100A" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.100A');">18.100A</a>, <a href="/search/?P=18.100B" title="18.100B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.100B');">18.100B</a>, or 18.100C
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">Acad Year 2016-2017: Not offered<br/>
Acad Year 2017-2018: G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Core analytical issues of continuous optimization, duality, and saddle point theory, and development using a handful of unifying principles that can be easily visualized and readily understood. Discusses in detail the mathematical theory of convex sets and functions which are the basis for an intuitive, highly visual, geometrical approach to the subject. Convex optimization algorithms focus on large-scale problems, drawn from several types of applications, such as resource allocation and machine learning. Includes batch and incremental subgradient, cutting plane, proximal, and bundle methods.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>D. P. Bertsekas
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.254 Game Theory with Engineering Applications</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">Acad Year 2016-2017: Not offered<br/>
Acad Year 2017-2018: G (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to fundamentals of game theory and mechanism design with motivations for each topic drawn from engineering applications (including distributed control of wireline/wireless communication networks, transportation networks, pricing). Emphasis on the foundations of the theory, mathematical tools, as well as modeling and the equilibrium notion in different environments. Topics include normal form games, supermodular games, dynamic games, repeated games, games with incomplete/imperfect information, mechanism design, cooperative game theory, and network games.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>A. Ozdaglar
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">

<p class="courseblockextra">

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.256 Algebraic Techniques and Semidefinite Optimization</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.251" title="6.251[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.251');">6.251[J]</a> or <a href="/search/?P=6.255" title="6.255[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.255');">6.255[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">Acad Year 2016-2017: Not offered<br/>
Acad Year 2017-2018: G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Theory and computational techniques for optimization problems involving polynomial equations and inequalities with particular, emphasis on the connections with semidefinite optimization. Develops algebraic and numerical approaches of general applicability, with a view towards methods that simultaneously incorporate both elements, stressing convexity-based ideas, complexity results, and efficient implementations. Examples from several engineering areas, in particular systems and control applications. Topics include semidefinite programming, resultants/discriminants, hyperbolic polynomials, Groebner bases, quantifier elimination, and sum of squares.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>P. Parrilo
</i></span></p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.262 Discrete Stochastic Processes</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.431B" title="6.431B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.431B');">6.431B</a> or <a href="/search/?P=18.204" title="18.204" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.204');">18.204</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Review of probability and laws of large numbers; Poisson counting process and renewal processes; Markov chains (including Markov decision theory), branching processes, birth-death processes, and semi-Markov processes; continuous-time Markov chains and reversibility; random walks, martingales, and large deviations; applications from queueing, communication, control, and operations research.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>R. G. Gallager, V. W. S. Chan
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.263[J] Data-Communication Networks</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=16.37J" title="16.37[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '16.37J');">16.37[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a> or <a href="/search/?P=18.204" title="18.204" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.204');">18.204</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">Acad Year 2016-2017: Not offered<br/>
Acad Year 2017-2018: G (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Provides an introduction to data networks with an analytic perspective, using telephone networks, wireless networks, optical networks, the Internet and data centers as primary applications. Presents basic tools for modeling and performance analysis accompanied by elementary, meaningful simulations. Develops insights for large networks by means of simple approximations. Draws upon concepts from queueing theory and optimization.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>E. Modiano, D. Shah
</i></span></p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.267 Heterogeneous Networks: Architecture, Transport, Proctocols, and Management</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a> or <a href="/search/?P=6.042" title="6.042[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.042');">6.042[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">Acad Year 2016-2017: Not offered<br/>
Acad Year 2017-2018: G (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to modern heterogeneous networks and the provision of heterogeneous services. Architectural principles, analysis, algorithmic techniques, performance analysis, and existing designs are developed and applied to understand current problems in network design and architecture. Begins with basic principles of networking. Emphasizes development of mathematical and algorithmic tools; applies them to understanding network layer design from the performance and scalability viewpoint. Concludes with network management and control, including the architecture and performance analysis of interconnected heterogeneous networks. Provides background and insight to understand current network literature and to perform research on networks with the aid of network design projects.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>V. W. S. Chan, R. G. Gallager
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.268 Network Science and Models</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a>, <a href="/search/?P=18.06" title="18.06" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.06');">18.06</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">Acad Year 2016-2017: G (Spring)<br/>
Acad Year 2017-2018: Not offered
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduces the main mathematical models used to describe large networks and dynamical processes that evolve on networks. Static models of random graphs, preferential attachment, and other graph evolution models. Epidemic propagation, opinion dynamics, social learning, and inference in networks. Applications drawn from social, economic, natural, and infrastructure networks, as well as networked decision systems such as sensor networks.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. N. Tsitsiklis, P. Jaillet
</i></span></p>
</div><h3 class="subsection">Electronics, Computers, and Systems</h3><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.301 Solid-State Circuits</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.012" title="6.012" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.012');">6.012</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-2-7 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Analysis and design of transistor circuits, based directly on the semiconductor physics and transistor circuit models developed in <a href="/search/?P=6.012" title="6.012" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.012');">6.012</a>. High-frequency and low-frequency design calculations and simulation of multistage transistor circuits. Trans-linear circuits. Introduction to operational-amplifier design and application. Some previous laboratory experience assumed.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>H. S. Lee
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.302 Feedback System Design</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Subject meets with <a href="/search/?P=6.320" title="6.320" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.320');">6.320</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.003" title="6.003" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.003');">6.003</a>, <a href="/search/?P=2.003" title="2.003[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '2.003');">2.003[J]</a>, or <a href="/search/?P=16.002" title="16.002" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '16.002');">16.002</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">U (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-2-6 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Learn-by-design introduction to continuous and discrete-time system modeling and feedback control. Topics include performance metrics; time- and frequency-domain model extraction and classical control; and basic state-space control. Students apply the control concepts in weekly labs and in a midterm project. Labs involve designing circuits and software, and using sensors and a high-performance microcontroller, to address control problems, such as positioning a motor- or propeller-actuated robot arm, reducing distortion in a PWM-based audio amplifier, eliminating field crosstalk for a magnetic-resonance imager, stabilizing magnetic levitation, balancing a two-wheel vehicle. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments and an extra lab on observer-based state-space control. Intended for students who have previous laboratory experience with electronic systems.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. D. Steinmeyer, J. K. White
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.336[J] Introduction to Numerical Simulation</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=2.096J" title="2.096[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '2.096J');">2.096[J]</a>, <a href="/search/?P=16.910J" title="16.910[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '16.910J');">16.910[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=18.03" title="18.03" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.03');">18.03</a> or <a href="/search/?P=18.06" title="18.06" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.06');">18.06</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-3-6 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to computational techniques for the simulation of a large variety of engineering and physical systems. Applications are drawn from aerospace, mechanical, electrical, chemical engineering, biology, and materials science. Topics include mathematical formulations (techniques for automatic assembly of mathematical problems from physics' principles); sparse, direct and iterative solution techniques for linear systems; Newton and Homotopy methods for nonlinear problems; discretization methods for ordinary, time-periodic and partial differential equations; accelerated methods for integral equations; techniques for automatic generation of compact dynamical system models and model order reduction.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>L. Daniel, J. K. White
</i></span></p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.341 Discrete-Time Signal Processing</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.011" title="6.011" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.011');">6.011</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Representation, analysis, and design of discrete time signals and systems. Decimation, interpolation, and sampling rate conversion. Noise shaping. Flowgraph structures for DT systems. Lattice filters. Time- and frequency-domain design techniques for IIR and FIR filters. Parametric signal modeling, linear prediction, and the relation to lattice filters. Discrete Fourier transform (DFT). Computation of the DFT including FFT algorithms. Short-time Fourier analysis and relation to filter banks. Multirate techniques. Perfect reconstruction filter banks and their relation to wavelets.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>A. V. Oppenheim, J. Ward
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.344 Digital Image Processing</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.003" title="6.003" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.003');">6.003</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Digital images as two-dimensional signals. Digital signal processing theories used for digital image processing, including one-dimensional and two-dimensional convolution, Fourier transform, discrete Fourier transform, and discrete cosine transform. Image processing basics. Image enhancement. Image restoration. Image coding and compression. Video processing including video coding and compression. Additional topics including digital high-definition television systems.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>J. S. Lim
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.345[J] Automatic Speech Recognition</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockcluster">Same subject as <a href="/search/?P=HST.728J" title="HST.728[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, 'HST.728J');">HST.728[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.011" title="6.011" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.011');">6.011</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.036" title="6.036" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.036');">6.036</a>

Acad Year 2017-2018: Not offered
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-1-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduces the rapidly developing fields of automatic speech recognition and spoken language processing. Topics include acoustic theory of speech production, acoustic-phonetics, signal representation, acoustic and language modeling, search, hidden Markov modeling, deep neural networks, system robustness, adaptation, and other related speech processing topics. Lecture material intersperses theory with practice. Includes problem sets, laboratory exercises, and opened-ended term project.

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.374 Analysis and Design of Digital Integrated Circuits</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.012" title="6.012" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.012');">6.012</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.004" title="6.004" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.004');">6.004</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-3-6 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Device and circuit level optimization of digital building blocks. MOS device models including Deep Sub-Micron effects. Circuit design styles for logic, arithmetic, and sequential blocks. Estimation and minimization of energy consumption. Interconnect models and parasitics, device sizing and logical effort, timing issues (clock skew and jitter), and active clock distribution techniques. Memory architectures, circuits (sense amplifiers), and devices. Testing of integrated circuits. Extensive custom and standard cell layout and simulation in design projects and software labs.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>V. Sze, A. P. Chandrakasan
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.375 Complex Digital Systems Design</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.004" title="6.004" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.004');">6.004</a>

Acad Year 2017-2018: G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">5-5-2 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to the design and implementation of large-scale digital systems using hardware description languages and high-level synthesis tools in conjunction with standard commercial electronic design automation (EDA) tools. Emphasizes modular and robust designs, reusable modules, correctness by construction, architectural exploration, meeting area and timing constraints, and developing functional field-programmable gate array (FPGA) prototypes. Extensive use of CAD tools in weekly labs serve as preparation for a multi-person design project on multi-million gate FPGAs.
Enrollment may be limited.</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>Arvind
</i></span></p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.437 Inference and Information</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.008" title="6.008" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.008');">6.008</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a>, or <a href="/search/?P=6.436" title="6.436[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.436');">6.436[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to principles of Bayesian and non-Bayesian statistical inference. Hypothesis testing and parameter estimation, sufficient statistics; exponential families. EM agorithm. Log-loss inference criterion, entropy and model capacity. Kullback-Leibler distance and information geometry. Asymptotic analysis and large deviations theory. Model order estimation; nonparametric statistics. Computational issues and approximation techniques; Monte Carlo methods. Selected special topics such as universal prediction and compression.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>P. Golland, G. W. Wornell
</i></span></p>

<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.438 Algorithms for Inference</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.008" title="6.008" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.008');">6.008</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a>, or <a href="/search/?P=6.436" title="6.436[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.436');">6.436[J]</a>; <a href="/search/?P=18.06" title="18.06" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '18.06');">18.06</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Fall)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">4-0-8 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduction to statistical inference with probabilistic graphical models. Directed and undirected graphical models, and factor graphs, over discrete and Gaussian distributions; hidden Markov models, linear dynamical systems. Sum-product and junction tree algorithms; forward-backward algorithm, Kalman filtering and smoothing. Min-sum and Viterbi algorithms. Variational methods, mean-field theory, and loopy belief propagation. Particle methods and filtering. Building graphical models from data, including parameter estimation and structure learning; Baum-Welch and Chow-Liu algorithms. Selected special topics.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>P. Golland, G. W. Wornell, D. Shah
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.440 Essential Coding Theory</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.006" title="6.006" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.006');">6.006</a>, <a href="/search/?P=6.045" title="6.045[J]" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.045');">6.045[J]</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">Acad Year 2016-2017: Not offered<br/>
Acad Year 2017-2018: G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Introduces the theory of error-correcting codes. Focuses on the essential results in the area, taught from first principles. Special focus on results of asymptotic or algorithmic significance. Principal topics include construction and existence results for error-correcting codes; limitations on the combinatorial performance of error-correcting codes; decoding algorithms; and applications to other areas of mathematics and computer science.
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>Staff
</i></span></p>
</div><div class="courseblock">
<h4 class="courseblocktitle"><span font="Meta Pro"><strong>6.441 Information Theory</strong></span></h4>
<p class="courseblockextra">
<span class="courseblockprereq">Prereq: <a href="/search/?P=6.041B" title="6.041B" class="bubblelink code" onclick="return showCourse(this, '6.041B');">6.041B</a>
</span><br/><span class="courseblockterms">G (Spring)
</span><br/><span class="courseblockhours">3-0-9 units</span>
</p>

<p class="courseblockdesc">Mathematical definitions of information measures, convexity, continuity, and variational properties. Lossless source coding; variable-length and block compression; Slepian-Wolf theorem; ergodic sources and Shannon-McMillan theorem. Hypothesis testing, large deviations and I-projection. Fundamental limits of block coding for noisy channels: capacity, dispersion, finite blocklength bounds. Coding with feedback. Joint source-channel problem. Rate-distortion theory, vector quantizers. Advanced topics include Gelfand-Pinsker problem, multiple access channels, broadcast channels (depending on available time).
</p>
<p class="courseblockinstructors seemore"><span><i>M. Medard, Y. Polyanskiy, L. Zheng
</i></span></p>
